## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) — nonlinear/forced/damped oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state (x, v) and possibly time t, which is the standard form of second-order ODE oscillator models. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly combine a restoring force term in x, damping in v, and optional external/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = c0 * x (small oscillations, sign of c0 typically negative)
- Linear viscous damping + restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped linear oscillator)
- Time-driven forcing added: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (externally forced oscillator)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sign(v) (sliding/friction-dominated damping)
- Quadratic (aero) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag-like dissipation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (nonlinear resonance, bistability)
- Pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = c0 * sin(x) + c1 * v (finite-angle pendulum with damping)
- Soft saturation of restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (bounded force/actuator saturation approximation)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * x (self-excited oscillations; typically c0*(1-x^2)*v - x form)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v + c3 * x (self-excitation via nonlinear damping in v)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x + c4 * v (Mathieu-type behavior/parametric resonance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring forces in oscillators are often odd functions of x (e.g., c*x, c*sin(x), c*x + c*x**3), reflecting left-right symmetry of the potential.
- Conservative (undamped, unforced) oscillators typically have dv_dt depending on x only; explicit v terms indicate dissipation or self-excitation.
- Linear damping appears as c*v; nonlinear damping often shows as v*Abs(v) (quadratic) or (c0 + c1*x**2)*v / (c0 + c1*v**2)*v (state-dependent).
- External periodic driving shows up as additive sin/cos terms in t; multiple harmonics (cos(c*t)+cos(2*c*t)) suggest nonlinear response/forcing complexity.
- Parametric resonance is suggested when x is multiplied by a periodic function of t, i.e., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x.
- Hardening/softening stiffness is indicated by cubic terms in x (x**3); sign changes in the cubic coefficient change frequency-amplitude behavior.
- Dry friction is suggested by sign(v) (or v/Abs(v)) terms, producing stick-slip-like non-smooth dynamics.
- Saturating elements in mechanisms/actuators commonly induce tanh(c*x) or sin(x) style bounded restoring terms, preventing unbounded acceleration at large |x|.
- Self-oscillation (limit cycles) often requires negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, captured by (c0 + c1*x**2)*v with opposite signs across amplitude.

Candidate formulas: 61

GT (fixed):
\[
-0.194830767863936\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;3.04923978373096\,x e^{-|x|}\;-\;0.143047751034959\sin(v)
\]
Rewrite:
\[
(-0.194830767863936)\,v \;+\; (0.194830767863936)\,v x^2 \;+\; (-3.04923978373096)\,x e^{(-1)|x|}\;+\;(-0.143047751034959)\sin(1\cdot v)
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent exactly these four terms and **no others**:
- linear \(v\) term
- \(v x^2\) term
- \(\sin(v)\) term (phase shift allowed, but must reduce to \(\sin(v)\) exactly)
- \(x\exp(-|x|)\) term (must have exponent coefficient \(-1\) on \(|x|\))
and must have **no** \(t\)-dependence, no constants, no \(v^3,v^5\), no extra nonlinearities like \(v/(c+|v|)\), \(v|v|\), logs, etc. (unless their coefficients can be set to 0).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can set its free constants to obtain exactly the GT.

---

### 1.
Has many extra terms: \(v^3, v^5,\) constant, and also a bare “\(+v\)” plus \(c1 v\). We can set \(c0=c7=c5=0\) and \(c6\) for \(vx^2\), \(c8 x\exp(c9|x|)\) with \(c9=-1\), and choose sine params. But there is an unavoidable extra \(+v\) term; we can absorb it by choosing \(c1\) so that \((c1+1)v\) matches GT’s \(-0.1948 v\). So linear \(v\) is OK. Constant \(c5\) can be 0. Sine can match \(-0.1430\sin(v)\) by \(c2=-0.1430, c3=1, c4=0\). Thus candidate 1 **can** match GT.

Form: \(c0 v + c1 v^3 + c2\sin(c3 v+c4)+ c5 v x^2 + c6 v^5 + c7 x e^{c8|x|}+c9\).

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.194830767863936*v*(1 - x**2) - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

Expanding the GT:
`-0.194830767863936*v + 0.194830767863936*v*x**2 - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

So the GT has these basis functions:
1. `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.1948)
2. `v*x**2` (coefficient ≈ 0.1948)
3. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` (coefficient ≈ -3.0492)
4. `sin(v)` (coefficient ≈ -0.1430)

No constant term, no `v**3`, no `v**5`, no `t` dependence, no `v*Abs(v)`, no other exotic terms.

Let me check each candidate for whether it can reduce to exactly these four basis functions (plus possibly a zero constant).

**Key structural requirements:**
- Must have `v`, `v*x**2`, `x*exp(c*Abs(x))`, and `sin(v)` (possibly as `sin(c+c*v)`)
- Extra terms must be eliminable (set coefficients to 0)
- `sin(c2 + c3*v)` with `c3=1` gives `sin(c2+v) = sin(c2)cos(v) + cos(c2)sin(v)`, which introduces `cos(v)` unless `c2=0` or `c2=nπ`. With `c2=0`: `sin(v)` ✓

Let me systematically check:

For candidates with `sin(c2 + c3*v)`: set `c2=0, c3=1` to get `sin(v)`.

For candidates with `v**3`, `v**5`: need coefficient = 0.

For candidates with `exp(c*v)`: set `c4=0` gives a constant, absorbable into constant term.

For candidates with `t` terms: need coefficient = 0.

For candidates with `v*Abs(v)`: this is NOT equivalent to `v**2` or any polynomial in `v` — it equals `v²` for `v>0` and `-v²` for `v<0`. Cannot be zeroed unless coefficient = 0.

For candidates with `log(c*v+1)`: problematic for negative `v`. Set coefficient to 0.

For candidates with extra `+v` terms: absorbed into the `v` coefficient.

Let me now go through each:

**Candidates that have exactly {v, v*x², x*exp(c*Abs(x)), sin(v)} plus eliminable terms:**

- **Candidate 1:** `c0*v**3 + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v+c4) + c5 + c6*v*x**2 + c7*v**5 + c8*x*exp(c9*Abs(x)) + v` — Set c0=0, c7=0, c5=0, c4=0, c3=1. Remaining: `(c1+1)*v + c2*sin(v) + c6*v*x² + c8*x*exp(c9*Abs(x))` ✓

Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

- **Candidate 2:** `c0*v + c1*v**3 + c2*sin(c3*v+c4) + c5*v*x**2 + c6*v**5 + c7*x*exp(c8*Abs(x)) + c9` — Set c1=0, c6=0, c9=0, c4=0, c3=1. ✓

Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

- **Candidate 3:** Same as 2 without constant. Set c1=0, c6=0, c4=0, c3=1. ✓

Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

- **Candidate 4:** Has `c8*v/(c9+Abs(v))`. This is NOT a standard basis function and cannot be expressed as a linear combination of {v, v*x², sin(v), x*exp(-Abs(x))}. Setting c8=0 eliminates it. Then: `c0*v + c1*sin(c2+c3*v) + c4*v*x² + c5*x*exp(c6*Abs(x)) + c7`. Set c7=0, c2=0, c3=1. ✓
